< review>
Amazing little sushi restaurant, literally a hidden gem of Palo Alto since it's not on the street front but hidden behind in an alley.
Super fresh fish and the chef delicately dresses up every single piece of nigiri keeping the flavors in mind.
The uni was one of the freshest we've had in the bay area and some of the other stars included kanpachi, Shima aji, kin medai, sake to, Umi masu and of course the toro!<//review>

<Text>Overall: super fresh, super tasty (can be expensive)

FOOD: omg, wow. So good . Every piece of nigiri was absolutely amazing. We had an assortment of fish and seriously, every single piece was delicious. My favorites were the toro, uni, salmon belly. But seriously all were great. I have to say that I was very impressed by how fresh everything was and the presentation of the food was still excellent.

LOCATION/SERVICE: a little hard to find lol. It's like in an alley and I only found it because of a sidewalk sign. The restaurant was clean and had great service. People there were very friendly and on top of it. We got our food quickly.

Would recommend if looking for delicious sushi and willing to pay</Text></record>

< Review>
This place was great! My wife and I have been to a handful of sushi places in the area and this one hit the spot! The waitress was very helpful and attentive, and overall the service was fast and excellent. We ordered several rolls and enjoyed all of them. They have a good selection of options but without being overwhelming. The presentation, freshness, and taste were great, especially for a pretty reasonable price. We'll definitely be going back. The place is small but very well decorated and clean. It's a small hidden gem.< /Review>

< text>
Finally authentic nigiri and sashimi in Palo Alto. Daigo replaces long time favorite and casual takeout spot Homma‚Äôs Brown Rice sushi with a more upscale and traditional sushiya experience.  Despite not being Japanese run, Daigo impresses with an extensive specials menu (rivals Gintei in San Bruno) and solid knife skills.  Nigiri are priced per piece which means prices can add quickly but that you can also sample a lot of variety.
Tip: order from the specials menu or choose among a variety of Omakase specials where the chef will choose.</text>

< Review>
Checked out this place on a quiet Sunday during their soft open. Second branch of a popular SF spot. Wait staff was lovely and attentive and the co-owner was so welcoming and friendly, recommending a perfectly clean tasting sake and making us feel as if we'd sat down to dinner at a friend's house (who just happens to make amazing sushi). Sashimi was delicious and fresh, flown in from Japan daily! They will add omakase and other specials eventually. Rolls were on point, good balance of filling v. rice, great flavor, and easy to fit in my mouth. Get the tamago too, it was just oozing with umami. We got comped a tasty green tea cheesecake for dessert! All in all a satisfying meal and I'm looking forward to making this my regular sushi spot.<//Review>

I have been out to this location twice. The first time, a reasonably busy Friday night, I sat at the bar by myself like I frequently do, and had a nice experience. The bar staff was attentive, the daily tacos were excellent, and I left with the idea cemented into my head that I would be back again. The second experience nearly ruined it for me. The bar tender that night was completely oblivious, entirely submerged in a nearly hour long conversation with a couple just three seats down from me, and failed to even ask me if I would like another drink when mine was empty; another one of the bar staff picked up the slack for him. He then proceeded to brag to this couple that he was the "best bar tender in Orange County", a claim that I, to be kind, scoffed at. I believe his name was Paul. I will probably be back to this location, simply due to the quality of food and draft beer selection so close to my temporary home, but I doubt I'll ever forget the impeccable lack of service I received that evening.</Text>

<Rating>1<//Rating>< Text>
Can't say how disappointed I was in the service and the food we received on the night of 3/25/2017.

Upon entering the restaurant, my wife and I were the first out of a party of 4 to get there. We stood around waiting for someone to seat us and was rather annoyed that out of the 3 servers and the one bartender, we were being unnoticed. I eventually had to walk up to a server and ask if anyone was going to seat us. Mind you, the establishment was not overly busy at the time. Strike one.

A few minutes later, our other two guests arrived.  Our server gave us some waters and had us look over the menu. One of our guests asks the server if she could sample a beer. It was super awkward when the sever questioned the sampling of a beer. There was a moment of pause and a bewildered look to the servers face.  It couldn't be more obvious that the server was shocked that someone wanted a sample of a beer.  I wanted a lighter beer and a Pacifico sounded good. The server came back and told me that they were out of Pacifico. Who runs out of Pacifico?  Really?  Strike two.

Upon ordering our dinner, the server fesses up that it's her second day on the job and that this restaurant is different than her last. Okay, I get it, I understand. I've worked in a restaurant before and I know how hectic it can be.  This note is for the manager there, if there is one. If you have a new server who doesn't seem like they know what they are doing, perhaps it would behoove you to have your other employees help them out. It would make your patron's experience much better, and perhaps would make your employees much happier in the long run.  So we order our food and my wife decides on the short rib. The server then asks how does she want it cooked?  Is that a trick question?  No, she was serious.  We finally get our food and everyone's dinner looks okay with the exception of my wife's short rib. It came out grey, super dry, and lacking of all flavor. We send it back and order their grilled cheese. Literally it takes them almost 20 minutes to make it and they forgot the bacon. Whatever at this point. Strike three.

Lastly, please ensure the restrooms have an adequate supply of paper towels.

Go at your own risk.< /Text>

<response>None<//response>< Text>
Duck Fat Fried Chicken and Waffles ($17) is served with maple butter and crow hot sauce. The exterior is golden brown and crispy. The duck fat flavor is definitely apparent and adds a richness to the chicken. The chicken is tender and juicy. The waffle is pretty good, but adding the maple butter and syrup makes it a winner. The hot sauce gives it a spicy kick to get you going on a Sunday morning. Rating: 4.8/5

The Crow "Black Label" Burger ($19) is an 8 oz. signature blend beef patty (including 21 day dry aged prime ribeye) served on a brioche bun with bone marrow butter, and caramelized onions. The burger patty is juicy and meaty. The bone marrow butter adds a creamy richness to the burger and caramelized onions add sweetness. The brioche bun is soft yet sturdy and holds the juices in the burger. Add a side of duck fat fries. The fries have a crispy exterior and kettle chip flavor with a soft, fluffy interior. Rating: 4.8/5

"Smores" ($10) is a graham cracker cake topped with milk chocolate and toasted marshmallow ice cream. The cake has a solid texture, almost like cornbread. It has an in-your-face graham cracker flavor. The marshmallow ice cream is creamy, fluffy, and tastes like ice cold marshmallow cr√®me. Hershey's chocolate mini bars are at room temperature so it is slightly soft for a melt-in-your-mouth s'mores experience. All that is missing is a little bit of burned sugar! Rating: 3.5/5</Text>
